    "besides their fundamental role in mathematics , lie algebras are of central importance in many areas of physics . the lie algebra @xmath3 describes rotations in 3-dimensional",
    "coordinate space as well as in the isospin space of nuclear and particle physics .",
    "the lie algebra @xmath1 describes the extension of isospin to the flavor symmetries of up , down , and strange quarks @xcite , and also represents the color degree of freedom by which quarks couple to the non - abelian gluon gauge field @xcite .",
    "the exceptional lie algebra @xmath2 contains @xmath1 as a subalgebra and has been used in early attempts to generalize flavor symmetries @xcite .",
    "the algebra @xmath2 also plays a role in the context of supersymmetry and string theory @xcite .",
    "the group @xmath4 has a trivial center , which makes non - abelian @xmath4 lattice gauge theories an interesting theoretical laboratory for studying confinement and deconfinement @xcite .",
    "the group @xmath5 , which is the universal covering group of @xmath6 , has the non - trivial center @xmath7 .",
    "for this reason , confinement and deconfinement have also been studied in @xmath8 non - abelian gauge theories @xcite .",
    "furthermore , the algebra @xmath0 has been used in condensed matter physics in attempts to unify the order parameters of antiferromagnetism and high - temperature superconductivity @xcite .",
    "this is certainly just an incomplete list of physics applications of the simple rank 2 lie algebras . in all these and many other applications , it is vital to reduce tensor products of irreducible representations into sums of such representations .    for the algebras @xmath9 , @xmath10 , and",
    "@xmath11 there are useful schemes for tensor product reduction based on young tableaux @xcite .",
    "while these develop their full strength for larger values of @xmath12 , they are not the most economical schemes for @xmath0 or @xmath1 .",
    "instead antoine and speiser have described a graphical method that offers a particularly efficient approach to tensor product reduction for the rank 2 lie algebras @xmath0 , @xmath1 , and @xmath2 @xcite . for this purpose the weight diagram of an irreducible representation is placed in a 2-dimensional `` landscape '' of irreducible representations , centered at its tensor product partner . taking into account the `` parity '' @xmath13 of the various sectors of the landscape , the degeneracies of the states in the weight diagram then determine the multiplicity with which a given irreducible representation appears in the tensor product reduction .",
    "an algebraic variant of the graphical method uses so - called `` girdles '' , which are polynomials associated with each irreducible representation @xcite . by multiplying the girdles and decomposing their product into sums of girdles",
    ", one then determines the tensor product decomposition of the corresponding irreducible representations .",
    "compared to the girdle method , the graphical scheme is very intuitive and easy to use by hand for moderately large representations , for which the girdle method is already very cumbersome . when implemented with automated computer codes , which becomes necessary for very large representations ,",
    "the computational effort of both methods is more or less the same . while one of the authors has used the graphical antonie - speiser scheme for @xmath1 for several decades , we are unaware of places in the literature where the method is worked out in sufficient detail to facilitate practical applications .",
    "we are also unaware of practical applications of the method to the other rank 2 lie algebras @xmath0 and @xmath2 .",
    "let us first illustrate the antoine - speiser scheme in the simple case of @xmath14 .",
    "the group @xmath15 has the center @xmath16 , consisting of plus and minus the @xmath17 unit - matrix , which obviously commute with all @xmath15 group elements . correspondingly , there are two different types of irreducible representations of the @xmath3 algebra , those with integer and those with half - integer spin .",
    "the integer spin @xmath18 representations @xmath19 have trivial `` duality '' and contain an odd number of @xmath20 states , which are distinguished by their spin projection @xmath21 .",
    "the half - integer spin representations , on the other hand , have non - trivial duality and contain an even number of @xmath20 states .",
    "in contrast to other lie algebras , all states in an @xmath3 representation are non - degenerate and thus have different values of @xmath22 .",
    "we introduce @xmath23 and alternatively denote a representation as @xmath24 . while this alternative notation may seem unnecessary for @xmath3 , it will be very natural for the higher - rank lie algebras . in the interest of a unified notation",
    "we therefore introduce @xmath25 already for @xmath3 .",
    "the dimension of the representation @xmath25 is then given by @xmath26 the weight diagrams of some small representations are illustrated in figs.[su2]a and b. the reduction of the tensor product of two @xmath3 representations with spin @xmath27 and spin @xmath28 results in all representations with a total spin @xmath18 between @xmath29 and @xmath30 , in integer steps , i.e. @xmath31 indeed the dimensions of the various representations match because one can easily show that @xmath32 tensor product reduction in @xmath3 is hence so simple that it does not really require a graphical method .",
    "still , in order to illustrate the antoine - speiser scheme in the simplest case , here we apply it to @xmath3 .",
    "fig.[su2]c shows the landscape of @xmath3 representations with a positive sector on the right and a negative sector on the left .",
    "the landscape consists of two sublattices associated with the integer and half - integer spin representations . in fig.[su2]d",
    "the weight diagram of the @xmath33 representation @xmath34 has been centered at the position of the @xmath35 representation @xmath36 in the landscape . the five states in @xmath34",
    "identify five representations in the landscape , which contribute with a positive or negative sign , depending on the sector they are in .",
    "this leads to the tensor product reduction @xmath37 which indeed corresponds to the total spins @xmath38 and @xmath39 .",
    "note that we have combined a trivial duality ( integer spin 2 ) representation with a non - trivial duality ( half - integer spin @xmath40 ) representation in the landscape , thus resulting in a sum of non - trivial duality ( half - integer spin ) representations in the tensor product reduction .",
    "the reader may want to copy the weight diagrams of figs.[su2]a and b on a transparency and perform further tensor product reductions by superimposing them on a partner representation in the landscape of fig.[su2]c .",
    "let us also illustrate the girdle method @xcite in the simple @xmath3 case .",
    "first of all , every representation @xmath41 is associated with a characteristic laurent polynomial ( containing both positive and negative powers ) @xmath42 for example , the characteristic laurent polynomials of the smallest representations are given by @xmath43 tensor product reductions of the representations @xmath44 and @xmath45 , i.e. @xmath46 are then determined from the product of the corresponding characteristic polynomials @xmath47 here @xmath48 is the multiplicity with which the representation @xmath25 contributes to the tensor product . for @xmath3 ( but not for the higher - rank lie algebras ) @xmath48",
    "is limited to 0 or 1 .",
    "interestingly , there is a more efficient way to determine the tensor product reduction , in which the characteristic laurent polynomials are replaced by ratios of simpler girdle polynomials @xmath49 the girdle polynomial is determined by the positions @xmath50 of the representation @xmath51 in the positive and negative sectors of the landscape .",
    "the girdles associated with the smallest representations are given by @xmath52 this trivially generalizes to all values of @xmath53 since @xmath54 expressed with girdles , the tensor product decomposition of eq.([redsu2 ] ) then simplifies to @xmath55 for example , the tensor product reduction of eq.([su2red52 ] ) then takes the form @xmath56 this again confirms that @xmath57 .    in this paper",
    ", we work out the antoine - speiser method in great detail for the three simple rank 2 lie algebras . in particular , we construct the landscapes for @xmath0 , @xmath1 , and @xmath2 , including relatively large representations .",
    "we also provide weight diagrams , including the degeneracy factors of the various states , for a large number of irreducible representations .",
    "this facilitates the tensor product reduction for a large variety of pairs of irreducible representations in a practical and efficient manner . by copying the weight diagrams on a transparency",
    ", the reader can easily work out rather complicated tensor product reductions by hand .",
    "we also discuss the girdle method , which is much more cumbersome for calculations with moderate - size representations by hand , but equivalent to the graphical method when implemented as an automated computer code .",
    "we provide software , available from the authors upon request , that implements the graphical antoine - speiser scheme and is applicable to very large irreducible representations .",
    "the three cases of @xmath0 , @xmath1 , and @xmath2 are treated in three subsequent sections 2 , 3 , and 4 .",
    "section 5 contains our conclusions .",
    "in this section , we work out the antoine - speiser scheme for the algebra @xmath58 which coincides with the algebra @xmath59 . after defining these algebras and their corresponding lie groups , we construct the weight diagrams of many irreducible representations as well as the corresponding landscape , which is 2-dimensional because the algebra @xmath0 has rank 2 .",
    "we then use the method of superimposing a weight diagram on the landscape in order to reduce the tensor product of two irreducible representations .",

    "we have worked out a graphical tensor product reduction scheme for the simple rank 2 lie algebras @xmath0 , @xmath1 , and @xmath2 , which relies on the fact that 2-dimensional weight diagrams can be superimposed on a 2-dimensional landscape of irreducible representations .",
    "while the method itself extends to algebras of higher rank , and thus to higher - dimensional weight diagrams and `` landscapes '' , in practice the method of superimposing them only works in one or two dimensions and is thus limited to rank 1 or 2 .",
    "we have also used the algebraic girdle method for tensor product reduction , which is much more tedious than the graphical method for calculations by hand even for small representations .",
    "furthermore , we have developed computer code for automated tensor product reduction , based on the graphical method .",
    "this code could be extended to higher - rank algebras in a straightforward manner .",
    "we dedicate this paper to the memory of petro i.  holod , who had a large impact as a teacher of group theory and lie algebras @xcite , motivating generations of students to aim at understanding nature at a deep level .",

  "abstract_text": [
    "<S> we develop in detail a graphical tensor product reduction scheme , first described by antoine and speiser , for the simple rank 2 lie algebras @xmath0 , @xmath1 , and @xmath2 . </S>",
    "<S> this leads to an efficient practical method to reduce tensor products of irreducible representations into sums of such representations . for this purpose , </S>",
    "<S> the 2-dimensional weight diagram of a given representation is placed in a `` landscape '' of irreducible representations . </S>",
    "<S> we provide both the landscapes and the weight diagrams for a large number of representations for the three simple rank 2 lie algebras . </S>",
    "<S> we also apply the algebraic `` girdle '' method , which is much less efficient for calculations by hand for moderately large representations . </S>",
    "<S> computer code for reducing tensor products , based on the graphical method , has been developed as well and is available from the authors upon request . </S>"
  ]
